1932735410|4.0|After deciding to get my PMP certification, I spent time reviewing the Certification process and coming-up with an attack plan. I gave myself a year from start-to-finish (from filling out the application to passing the test). I started in August of 2011.<br /><br />The process to get to the point of scheduling my exam took more energy than I had thought it would. Documenting my Projects, completing the Application, taking/documenting my Professional hours and becoming a local chapter PMP member seemed a bit grueling---but that is what was needed, so I did it.  At the end of December of 2011, my PMP Application was formally accepted and I was now in a position to schedule my Test. Phew! I had until December of 2012 to pass the Test (within 3 try's).<br /><br />I gave myself 8 weeks to study for the PMP---and scheduled the test for April 2012---which would give me some breathing room around the Holidays. But then work/life got in the way and it was March before I knew it and I had yet to open a book! I rescheduled for June---and then rescheduled for August.  I remade the committement to finishing (I only had until December to pass) and blocked off July and August as Study months.<br /><br />But what/how to Study? Before scheduling my Test (the first time), I read lots of reviews/searched many sites and finally settled on Rita Mulcahy's Prep Book/FastTrack Testbank. My plan was to complete Rita's book, read the PMBOK and then take 3 simulated Tests (Full, 4 hour long, 200 questions) using the FastTrack Software. I decided that I was going to spend at least 1-2 hours a night and every weekend studying. Additionally, if it was harder than I anticipated, I would take off Mondays over the 2 months and use those as extra study days.<br /><br />What actually happened was that it was harder than I thought it was going to be to study, grasp and memorize all of the information. (Which surprised me because I have a graduate degree and have been a Project Manager on multi-million dollar Projects for a fortune 500 company for 5 years. Go figure!) After the first week I kicked-in my backup Monday's and truly cleared my calendar for the full 2 months as much as possible---declining social events was a pain, but getting time from work was difficult with my current Project, but I had too or I knew I wouldn't pass.<br /><br />2 weeks into my Studying of Rita's book, I knew I had to do something different---the book format and amount of information was overwhelming me.  I went back to the web for more research to find another Approach and/or Study Materials.<br /><br />My first thought was to just bite-the-bullet and take a Prep Course (my company paid for all of my cost up to this point, but I knew they wouldn't pay for a Prep Course.) I found several  3-5 day, Instructor lead Prep Courses offered within 4 hours of me. I debated taking a weeks vacation and immersing myself in the material for a week. A quick calculation put the cost at about $2,500 when I factored in course & hotel---commuting wasn't an option because the courses were from 8am to 6 pm with some forms of homework. Setting aside the cost (which is no small amount) I had family and work committements that would suffer (and mentally distract me) if I went this route. I decided this wasn't the plan for me. I would choose a self-study course and if I didn't pass the first time I would re-evaluate a formal Prep course.<br /><br />After ruling out the formal prep course (at least for the first round of Testing), I focused on finding other study materials that might work better for me. (I was still at somewhat of a loss because I am typically a self guided, book/manual focused learner.) I decided I would get the 2nd option from my previous materials review--Andy Crowe's PMP Package (Book, Flash Cards, CD's and some Web Based Study Materials). I'm was well into week 3 when the study materials arrived. I opened the book and---Deja Vu. A bit easier for me to read/understand compared to Rita's but maybe it was just because I had already studied that material in Rita's book? Now what? I looked over the other material in Crowe's Package and found a 6 month on-line Access Key to their web site \\"Intuit\\"---can't hurt to try it...<br /><br />And there was the answer for me! On Andy Crowe's web site (\\"Intuit\\") there was an entire Self Guided, Video based presentation that mirrored/supplemented his book AND offered an on-line Test Bank. The entire presentation was long---50+ hours, I think, but it covered every facet of the PMBOK and was broken into manageable sections. Additionally, the material was presented in a very interesting/engaging format (well, as interesting as this material can be). I completed each section, read the book and then took the 20 question test from the book for each chapter. I was starting to feel like I could really do this!<br /><br />By the end of week 5 I had completed the on-line course and had read Crowe's book. I had also listened to the CD's---not very deep, but good context setting. I tried the flash cards but not much value to me.<br /><br />At this point, I had 3 weeks until my Test. I decided I was going to take three, 200 question/4 hour practice tests from the Intuit site----one every Monday. I would take the test (using the full 4 hours) and then review each answer---which was a great feature of the test bank in that it explained the right answer/told you why the other answers weren't correct. Unfortunately, to review all the questions/answers took my another 2-3 hours. A full day committement. Two weeks later, I had scored a 75% and then an 82%. Sweet! I'm feeling really good (dare I jinx myself and say Prepared?)<br /><br />On my last 'Study Monday', I decided to use Rita's FastTrack test bank---still taking the full test/studying the answers. Ugh: a 65% on the test! What the %^%}?!? The questions seemed a lot harder than Crowe's. Time to Panic! My test was Friday of that week (yesterday actually). I was worried that I didn't have much buffer between passing (61%) and my Studying. Now what? I decided to take off an extra day from work and take one last test from Rita's FastTrack, review the answers and then close the books. On Thursday I got a 74%. Closer. More buffer, but still not a lot of 'wiggle room'---especially If I'm stressed or the real test is harder....at this point, time was up and after a good nights sleep (sleeping pills did the trick!), I was off to my 9:00am PMP exam. (After doing a 'dry run' to find the location earlier in the week.)<br /><br />I arrived an hour early (just in case!), and did a last minute review of the 42 processes and the dozen formulas.  After checking in (I was assigned a locker/given a key, ID checked, an inspection of my pockets and a quick metal detector sweep), I sat in front of a monitor that had my Name/Test ready for me (my test site apparently offers all kinds of other test---there were two people taking CPA exams and someone taking an electrical test that I spoke too.) I started the tutorial and quickly made my way through it because I had read that I could use the 'extra' time to write down the information I wanted to make sure I didn't forget (or misremember) during the stress of testing. I'm glad I did! I was more nervous than I thought I would be and I had a hard time jotting it all down. [The tutorial was 15 minutes---it took my 5 minutes to get through it and then I took 10 minutes to write down the 42 processes (in Knowledge/Process grid) as well as all of the EV formulas.]<br /><br />The test was hard, no doubt about it: But I passed! Let me say that again: I'm officially a PMP!<br /><br />As for the Test: The first 3 questions I didn't know the answer---but I at least I knew the concepts. I forced myself to mark an answer and move on. The level of questions were more similar to Rita than Crowe's. Drat. That meant I had 'less buffer' if I believed my Prep test results. I focused on my Test Taking Strategy (answer every question, complete all questions in 3 hours--or less, take a 10 minute break and then review as many questions as possible). During my Prep Tests, I had run into the situation several times where I was feeling good about the testing but then I would come across a whole group of questions that I was unsure of the answers. As I chugged through the test I was feeling good---at least about getting enough questions right that I was passing, but I kept waiting for that group of question that would throw me off. I'm happy to say, I didn't run across that group during the test! In retrospect, there were about 5 questions where I didn't know the concepts---let alone the answer. I made educated guesses on those questions. The rest of the questions were very reflective of the testing questions from both Rita & Crowe---but I give Rita more credit on accuracy of Test questions. It took me longer to get through the actual test than it had during my Prep test. I could make it through all 200 questions in about 2 hours during my prior testing---it took a full three hours on the actual test.<br /><br />Bottom line: I spent a lot more time persuing my PMP than I first estimated I would need---in both completing the Application and Studying for the Exam. As for Study Materials: (1) Studying on Crowe's web site tutorial is my number one recommendation---again, for my learning style (2) Both books (Rita & Crowe's) were about equal for what they offered me in way of breaking down the PMBOK (3) Rita's FastTrack Test bank was more indicative of the level/style of questions.  ***Good Luck***didn't have much buffer between passing (61%) and my Studying. 0452287022|5.0|\\"It's a rare book that wins the battle against drooping eyelids,\\" (Tracy Chevalier). History, the beauty of art, and imagination all come together to keep the reader awake in Tracy Chevalier's novel, Girl with a Pearl Earring, as she opens the gates to a new perspective of a very famous painting.  Griet, \\"the wide-eyed maid\\" and protagonist, gives a voice to the girl in the portrait so many people admire.  After an unexpected accident with her father, she is forced to work as a maid for the very difficult Vermeer family.  Not only does she come to struggle with the new family and house, but she also toils with her feelings for Vermeer and the maid life.  Her beauty, brains, and outstanding artistic perspective set her apart from most other girls her age in Delft and cast her in an alluring light to Vermeer, the painter. Vermeer also draws Griet into his life in a painting and the only way they can express their love is through the world of art.  Love, loss, grief, debt, betrayal, lies, and friendship all come together in this one novel to tell the story of Griet and Vermeer's forbidden relationship during the 1660s in Delft, Holland.  Chevalier successfully manages to combine not only history and fiction, but also simplicity and detail, bringing the 1660s Delft life of the Girl with a Pearl Earring and Vermeer to the present day reader.<br />In case some do not know much about the painting of the Girl with a Pearl Earring by Vermeer, like I did, it is one of his most renowned paintings of his life and is famously known in art and history.  Sometimes referred to as \\"the Dutch Mona Lisa\\", the painting now sits in the Mauritshuis Gallery located in The Hague.  The story behind the painting, like the date or who the work was for, are uncertain. After I read the novel, because I was so interested in learning more, I tried to research the facts behind the painting and Vermeer.  However, there was little luck and the real history remains mostly a mystery.<br /> Since thereare no accurate references to rely on, Chavelier produced a fictional version of the historical moment when the painting was made.  With the novel's help, the painting now has a story so many people can admire and relish.  If you like Girl with a Pearl Earring, Falling Angels and The Virgin Blue are two other books by Chavelier.  Also, if you enjoyed The Other Boleyn Girl by Philippa Gregory, the Girl with a Pearl Earring is similar in style and is a historical fiction novel.<br /> I am a seventeen year old high school senior.  As an option of a novel for summer reading, I chose the Girl with a Pearl Earring.  I thoroughly enjoyed the novel from start to finish.  Though it is not a thriller, the forbidden quality of the novel lures the reader to curiosity.  The language also provides vivid images that allow me to truly feel that I am in the situation.  Chavelier also provides exquisite detail and creativity to a time where little history has been recorded.  Characters render personalities and characteristics that make it easy to depict with clarity.  Even though it is short time period, the journey is worth the read, just as the journey of the story that lead to the painting is just as important as the actual painting itself.

Lamora basically has many people after his life and has to try to dodge through various dangers, while attempting to keep his group together and in one piece. There are magical elements, extreme violence, a great deal of intrigue, action and edge of the seat excitement, as the author expertly weaves a complicated plot together. 0316017930|5.0|My high school class was assigned to read Outliers for our summer reading program. At first I was dreading reading the book because I have not read much non-fiction. However, the book pleasantly surprised me. By the end of the first chapter I could not put it down. Outliers is a great choice for anyone who wants a fascinating book to read.<br /><br />Outliers is a novel that explores how certain people in our society become so successful. The book itself is split up into two parts. The first focuses on opportunity and the second on legacy.<br /><br />In the beginning of the novel, Gladwell clearly states his intentions for the book as follows, \\"In Outliers, I want to convince you that these kinds of personal explanations of success don't work. People don't rise from nothing.\\" Gladwell, in Outliers, evaluates how some people become successful. Gladwell proposes that it is both our opportunities and legacies that help us to become who we are. Gladwell conveys, \\"The culture we belong to and legacies passed down by our forebears shape the patterns of our achievement in ways we cannot begin to imagine.\\" Through these cultural and legacy experiences, Gladwell explains the impact they have on us.<br /><br />In this fascinating book Gladwell takes you on a journey with some of the most successful people in the world. Through countless interviews and studies, Outliers explains how and why some people are successful and others who seem to have so much potential do not succeed.<br /><br />It can be rare to find a truly interesting and thought provoking non-fiction book. Outliers is a true outlier from you average every day book. For this reason, I would give this book five stars. Once you start reading, you will not be able to put the book down.

B006M4RN3U|4.0|I have been somewhat disillusioned with modern music, taking refuge in older bands like Genesis and Pink Floyd, in order to get any real depth out of music.  But when my brother-in-law insisted I look up the song \\"Some Nights\\", I did so, and found myself quite enjoying what I was hearing, despite the obvious pop leanings and especially the heavy auto-tuning near the end.  I did a bit of research and found they were the band that did \\"We Are Young\\".  Whoo boy, okay, that one is a bit overplayed, and it's okay, but I was kind of sick of that one.  But I was familiar with it, and decided to check out the album.<br />And I'm glad I did!  What I found was a pop album that strives to go beyond the simple bubblegum pop of most popular artists nowadays.  The album opens with Some Nights (Intro), an operatic piece that sounds simultaneously like classic Queen and My Chemical Romance's \\"The End\\" from The Black Parade (which itself was heavily influenced by Queen!) that in and of itself isn't much of a song but it serves as an excellent introduction to the album, giving the impression that big things are in store.  And by far, the first half of the album doesn't disappoint.  The aforementioned \\"Some Nights\\" follows, beginning with a harmonized vocal intro that somehow recalls the finely tuned gospel sound similar to that of the Backstreet Boys, without making me want to vomit all over myself.  It then goes into a tribal-rock beat while Nate Ruess discusses the effects of war on the people who are involved.<br />Next up is the song everyone knows, \\"We Are Young\\".  I have to say this is probably the lowest point of the first half; the lyrics are nice but the music is wanting, with the verse actually being musically superior to the chorus (musician's protip: don't do this).  I shouldn't have to say too much about this one; you've probably already heard it and have made your mind up about it.  However, don't let it discourage you from checking out the band anyway, as it gives something of a false impression.<br />After that is \\"Carry On\\", which sounds unassuming at first but takes on a new life a couple minutes in when the backing instruments kick in and bring a whole Irish folk vibe to the sound, at which point I simply fall in love with it.  And this basically ends the first half of the album.<br />And this is where things start to collapse under their own weight.  The next song is \\"It Gets Better\\", and it's so drastically sub-par it compels me to skip it almost every time.  It sounds like 90's Rush, if Neal Peart were a caveman (and I don't hold as high a regard for Neal Peart as many do), wrapped in a thick coat of Blink 182.  The end result is an obnoxious rock song that does absolutely nothing interesting.<br />Fortunately, this horrible display of inadequacy is made up for by the next two songs, which are a couple of my favorites.  \\"Why Am I The One\\" heavily recalls Electric Light Orchestra (the chorus sounds very much like \\"Sweet Is The Night\\" off ELO's Out Of The Blue album), though to be fair, it is very structurally unsophisticated, and some may find it boring.  However, the track that comes next, \\"All Alone,\\" is a great track, starting off with a catchy verse similar to Maroon 5's \\"This Love\\" before breaking into one of the catchiest choruses I've heard lately, despite the simplistic lyrics.<br />\\"One Foot\\" is another one I find obnoxious.  The background music repeats the same damn annoying horn riff endlessly while Ruess does his best Eminem impression, and it fails to ever rise above mediocrity.  Next is the nearly-seven-minute \\"Star\\", which I initially disliked, but I have grown to appreciate several parts of it, even the bizarre autotuning bit that escalates nearly into madness, but always keeps it subtle.  While I don't think it's the fitting climax or conclusion to the album, it's certainly not a bad song, and I think when given enough attention, there's a lot to like.<br />Closing the album is the bonus track \\"Out On TheTown\\".  It should probably have been stuck somewhere in the middle of the album, because it doesn't really fit at the end.  It's a decent pop song that can get stuck in your head, but it lacks any hooks to really sink it in good.<br />So despite the weaknesses of the second half of the album, the strength of the good tracks (and fortunately there's a good number of them) elevates this album above the crap of most modern pop music and damn near into the realm of art.  The band clearly wears its influences on its sleeve, but it's largely presented with tact and cleverness.  Highly recommended!

0743454537|5.0|\\"Traditionally, parents made decisions for a child, because presumably they are looking out for his or her best interests. But if they are blinded, instead, by the best interests of another one of their children, the system breaks down.\\"<br /><br />  Jodi Picoult's My Sister's Keeper tests every aspect of the family dynamic with the Fitzgerald family. In the story, which combines family drama, a court case that rivals To Kill a Mockingbird, and suspense up until the very end, 13-year old Anna Fitzgerald sues her parents for the rights to her body. Conceived in order to be a donor match for her leukemic sister, Anna takes her parents to court in order to avoid donating her kidney to save her sick sister Kate. Her motivation for pursuing the case and the family reactions that unfold drive the gripping plot of this novel.<br /><br /> Picoult weaves an engaging and suspenseful plot, deftly switching perspectives of the main characters in each chapter. By writing each chapter from the perspective of a different character, Picoult allows the reader to understand the diverse points of view and opinions of the characters, ranging from Anna and her family to the lawyer and guardian ad litem who work with her on the case. Each character is intricately developed, with plot twists, romance, and internal conflict. The story is masterfully constructed, transitioning among the various storytellers without confusing the reader.<br /><br /> My Sister's Keeper confronts many serious ethical questions, making the reader examine his or her own beliefs. This book handles topics such as family obligation, designer babies, organ donors, and the role of parents with sensitivity and an accurate portrayal of all sides of each argument. Every character acts in the way he or she feels is correct, but the decisions are never easy, as shown when Anna's father asks, \\"Can you tell me what the right answer is here? Because I don't know where to look for it. I know what's right. I know what's fair.But neither of those apply here.\\"<br /><br />  One of the main reasons I enjoyed My Sister's Keeper is that I appreciate books that make me think and challenge my ideas. Woven into the story are serious concepts about the family dynamic. I found myself changing my mind as I read, first siding with Anna, then her mother, then her sister. The little nuggets of philosophical wisdom in the book are thought-provoking and insightful. The only complaint I have with this novel is its conclusion. Though I understand Picoult's point in writing the ending the way she did, it left me feeling unfulfilled and a little frustrated. As a whole, however, I highly recommend this novel.

0099448599|3.0|This is the book on which the Johnny Depp movie THE NINTH GATE is based. Published in the 1990s, I bought it because Carlos Ruiz Zafon (THE SHADOW OF THE WIND) lists it as one of his favourite books. If Zafon is a 'disciple' of Perez-Reverte, I think the student has begun to outpace his teacher.<br /><br />The story centres on the quest for copies of a rare 17th-century volume called The Nine Doors, which contains a hidden code for summoning up the Devil. Lucas Corso, a sort of Jason Bourne for bibliophiles, is obsessed with Alexandre Dumas's THE THREE MUSKETEERS and becomes convinced that the scarred man and the 'femme fatale' who keep obstructing his quest are incarnations of Dumas's most famous villains: the Count of Rochefort and Milady de Winter. He also hooks up with a mysterious beauty who calls herself Irene Adler (the name of the one woman Sherlock Holmes fell for).<br /><br />It's an unusual piece of fiction that can mention Miss Marple and the Inquisition on the same page! But I found THE DUMAS CLUB a bit disappointing, as I did the film version. The cover blurb seems to promise something along the lines of a Gothic potboiler by Dennis Wheatley (best remembered for THE DEVIL RIDES OUT, although my own great favourite was STRANGE CONFLICT, battling Satanists on the Astral Plane). But Arturo Perez-Reverte is more influenced by Umberto Eco, I suspect, although he is not in Eco's league (is anybody?.<br /><br />THE DUMAS CLUB is more of a literary 'conundrum' than the Hammer Horror extravaganza I was hoping for. It takes a while for the pace to pick up, but the last chapters are both spooky and sparky.<br /><br />[Reviewer is the author of THE DROPOUT]

145162607X|5.0|There is something about Philippa Gregory's writing that is enthralling. I love it when a series takes on different perspectives so you get a more well-rounded view of all sides.<br /><br />I felt sorry for the Neville girls. How awful to be used for gain and raised to marry and solely to increase one's wealth. I think the author did a great job at making the girls female versions of their father. He thought he was doing the right thing, but switching sides is not the best way to achieve an end. There were so many needless deaths over the throne and to protect one's right to reign that it was appalling. I can't imagine living in constant fear like that.<br /><br />Anne's mother was perfectly hateful, too. She did not act like she cared for her daughters at all, but merely had her own interests at heart. I felt especially bad for Isabel when she was pregnant the first time. I found the doubt that her mother put in Anne's head about her husband quite sad, and then when things got convoluted in his relationship with his niece, well, let's just say ick to that. I pitied Anne because she felt the desire to give up at such a young age. But after so many needless losses on so many fronts, I don't blame her for wanting to go to sleep and never wake again.<br /><br />I found the whole belief regarding the Woodville's controlling men through witchcraft quite fascinating, but I can see where things that cannot be explained would be concluded that way. There were a lot of needless deaths over this as well. So much treachery and loss. Anyway, I love this series because it makes me think and the most profound conclusion of all was that the very thing Anne wanted most of her life seemed hollow in the end without love. Isn't that the truth? Great story. I read it quickly and it's over 400 pages long. That's a great novel!l!
